The eye cannot focus clearly, so objects appear blurry. Around the age of 40, most people start to notice this change in their vision. Presbyopia will then gradually worsen up until the age of 65. Presbyopia eventually affects almost everyone, so those who believe they are exempt because they have always had perfect vision are likely still out of luck. Presbyopia can cause difficulty focusing on close-up reading when it first manifests. Others who stare at nearby objects might get headaches or strain their eyes. - [Air Optix Plus HydraGlyde for Astigmatism 6 Pack](https://contactlens365.com/products/air-optix-plus-hydraglyde-for-astigmatism): Air Optix Plus HydraGlyde for Astigmatism Astigmatism is a common eye condition that causes blurred vision. Air Optix with HydraGlyde for astigmatism are monthly disposable contacts produced to treat astigmatism. They can be worn continuously for up to 7 days every day or 6 nights for 30 days before needing to be removed, discarded, and replaced with a new set of lenses. To ensure long-lasting lens surface moisture, these contacts feature two of Alcon's exclusive innovations: SmartShield® Technology and HydraGlyde Moisture Matrix Technology. The way SmartShield Technology works is to prevent the buildup of protein and lipid deposits on the lens surface. Using daily cosmetics, hand lotions and makeup removers can change lens parameters, but our technology helps them resist these changes. On the other hand, HydraGlyde Moisture Matrix helps maintain lens surface moisture levels throughout the day. In addition, in the production of these contact lenses, lotrafilcon B, a breathable lens material that allows oxygen to constantly pass through the lens to make the eyes look white, clear and healthy, is used. Historically, astigmatic-fitting contact lenses have been difficult to find due to the unusual curvature of the eye. This problem has been solved with Alcon's tried-and-true Precision Balance 8|4 lens design. To ensure the correct fit, this design features contour lines at 3, 6 and 9 o'clock that allow for flexible lens viewing from a variety of angles. It also includes two attachment points to keep the lens in place and prevent blurred vision. A common eye disorder called astigmatism causes the cornea to have irregular curves. The eye should have a ball-like shape. Light bends evenly as it enters the eye, allowing you to see the object you're looking at clearly. Due to the unequal curvature of the cornea, astigmatism causes light to bend more in one direction than the other. As a result, only part of the object is in focus. The majority of individuals with astigmatism are born with this condition, but the cause is unknown. Astigmatism can also develop as a result of an eye disorder, surgery, or injury. Because astigmatism symptoms take time to appear, it is very important to see an ophthalmologist if you observe changes in your vision. These contacts can be worn for up to 14 hours per pair before being discarded and changed out for new ones. These lenses have Acuvue's patented LACREON Technology, which permanently incorporates a water-holding component into the lens material that is comparable to that in real tears. Speak to your eye care provider about trying 1-Day Acuvue Moist Multifocal contacts if you have presbyopia and wish to replace your glasses with contacts. Presbyopia happens when the eye's lens starts to stiffen and lose flexibility with age. The eye cannot focus clearly, thus objects appear hazy. Around the age of 40, most people start to notice this change in their vision. Presbyopia will thereafter steadily worsen up until the age of 65. Presbyopia eventually affects almost everyone, so those who believe they are exempt because they have always had flawless vision are likely still out of luck. Presbyopia can cause difficulty focusing on close-up reading when it first manifests. Others who stare at close items could get headaches or strain their eyes. Acuvue 1-Day Moist Because multifocal contacts are soft disposable lenses, you should use the regular care method for such lenses. To begin, wash your hands with a mild soap, then pat dry with a cloth without lint. With your dominant hand's index finger, remove the first lens from the casing. Use a cleaning solution made especially for soft contacts to rinse it. Make sure the lens is not turned inside-out and check for tears or other debris. Pull down your lower eyelid using your dominant hand's middle finger. If required, pull your upper eyelid with the middle finger of your non-dominant hand. Place the lens on your eye gently while maintaining a straight face. Several blinks will help the lens to center. Continue by using the other lens. If you experience double vision when wearing multifocal contacts for the first time, don't freak out. After a few weeks of using multifocal contacts, this should become better as part of the adaptation process.

A common disorder of the eyes called astigmatism causes the cornea to have uneven curves. The eye should have a ball-like shape. Light uniformly bends as it enters the eye, allowing you to see the object you're looking at clearly. Due to the cornea's uneven curvature, astigmatism causes light to be bent more in one direction than another. Only a portion of the object is in focus as a result. The majority of astigmatic individuals are born with the condition, but the reason for this is unknown. Astigmatism can also develop as a result of an eye disorder, surgery, or injury. Since astigmatism symptoms take time to manifest, it's crucial to consult an eye doctor if you observe changes in your vision. Presbyopia occurs when the lens of the eye begins to harden and lose its flexibility with age. Objects appear blurry because the eye cannot focus clearly. Around the age of 40, most people begin to notice this change in their vision. Presbyopia will steadily worsen thereafter until age 65. Presbyopia eventually affects almost everyone, so those who believe they are exempt because they have always had perfect vision are probably still out of luck. When presbyopia first occurs, it can make it difficult to focus on close reading. Others who look at close objects may experience headaches or eye strain. Additionally, Bausch Lomb's patented Lo-Torque design keeps the lenses stable during use, making these contact lenses ideal for people with astigmatism who lead very active lifestyles. about astigmatism Astigmatism (astigmatism) is a common eye condition in which the cornea of the eye has misaligned curves. Ideally, the eye should be in the shape of a round ball. When light enters the eye, it bends evenly, allowing you to see exactly what you are looking at. In people with astigmatism, light rays are refracted more in one direction than in the other due to the incongruous curvatures of the cornea. Therefore, the focus is on only one part of the subject. Most people with astigmatism are born with astigmatism but don't know why. You can also develop astigmatism after an eye injury, eye disease, or eye surgery. Because astigmatism symptoms develop slowly, it's important to look for phenylketonuria if you notice any changes in your vision. Can you sleep with SofLens Toric contact lenses (SofLens 66 Toric)? Yes, you can sleep with the SofLens Toric (SofLens 66 Toric). Napping is okay, as the SofLens Toric (SofLens 66 Toric) is  for nighttime use (sleeping through the night). The term "digital eye strain," frequently referred to as "computer vision syndrome," describes a collection of eye and vision-related issues brought on by extended use of digital gadgets. A simpler definition of digital eye strain is the ocular pain experienced after spending several hours in front of a digital screen. Ocular and non-ocular symptoms are both brought on by digital eye strain. Eye fatigue, tears, blurred vision, burning sensations, redness, and double vision are examples of ocular symptoms. On the other hand, non-ocular symptoms include weariness in general, headaches, and shoulder and neck pain. Digital eye strain is a condition that affects 90% of people who use digital devices, but it is more common in persons who use two or more digital devices at once. Because Bausch + Lomb ULTRA 6 Pack contacts are soft disposable lenses, you should adhere to the usual care instructions. To begin, wash your hands with a mild soap, then pat dry with a cloth without lint. With your dominant hand's index finger, remove the first lens from the casing. Use a cleaning solution made especially for soft contacts to rinse it. Make sure the lens is not turned inside-out and check for any tears or debris. Pull down your lower eyelid using your dominant hand's middle finger. If required, pull your upper eyelid with the middle finger of your non-dominant hand. Place the lens on your eye gently while looking upward. Several blinks will help the lens to center. Do the same thing using the other lens. Your eyes should feel at ease and your vision should be clear if Bausch + Lomb ULTRA 6 Pack contacts are properly implanted. A common eye disorder called astigmatism causes the cornea to have irregular curves. The eye should have a ball-like shape. Light bends evenly as it enters the eye, allowing you to see the object you're looking at clearly. Due to the unequal curvature of the cornea, astigmatism causes light to bend more in one direction than the other. As a result, only part of the object is in focus. The majority of individuals with astigmatism are born with this condition, but the cause is unknown. Astigmatism can also develop as a result of eye trauma, eye disease, or eye surgery. Because astigmatism symptoms take time to appear, it is very important to see an ophthalmologist if you observe changes in your vision. Unlike other color lenses where the tint is printed on the surface, Air Optix Colors uses a sophisticated 3-in-1 Color Technology to ensure your eyes look deep, natural, and bright. 3-in-1 Color Technology: This unique design blends three rings of color—an outer ring to define the eye, a primary color to transform the shade, and an inner ring to add depth and brilliance. SmartShield® Technology: A ultra-thin protective layer that shields the lenses from irritating deposits (like proteins and lipids) all month long. This ensures the lenses stay clean and comfortable from Day 1 to Day 30. Superior Breathability: As part of the Air Optix family, these lenses allow up to 5x more oxygen to reach the cornea than traditional hydrogel color lenses. Say goodbye to red, tired-looking eyes. Why OASYS MAX? — A New Standard in Daily Contact Lenses for Astigmatism The average  spends 13+ hours a day on digital devices. That means less blinking, faster tear evaporation, and for people with astigmatism, significantly greater visual challenges. ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day for Astigmatism was built to meet those demands head-on with three industry-leading technologies working together in a single daily contact lens. Acuvue Oasys Daily Contact Lens — 3 Breakthrough Technologies 1. TearStable™ Technology — All-Day Moisture, All-Day Comfort Forget surface coatings that wear off by midday. TearStable™ isn’t a coating — it’s embedded throughout the entire lens matrix. By mimicking the key components of your natural tear film, TearStable™ locks in moisture from morning to evening. Whether you’re grinding through back-to-back video calls or working in an air-conditioned environment, your eyes stay hydrated and comfortable all day long. 2. OptiBlue™ Light Filter — Precision Clarity for the Digital Age Exclusive to the ACUVUE® OASYS MAX daily contact lens family, OptiBlue™ selectively filters blue-violet light — the type that scatters more inside the eye and causes glare, halos, and visual fatigue. The result is sharper contrast, cleaner edges, and noticeably reduced visual noise. Particularly impactful for astigmatism patients who are more prone to night driving discomfort and sensitivity to bright LED headlights. 3. Cylinder Optimized BLINK STABILIZED® Design — Built for Astigmatism A genuine first in daily contact lenses. ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day for Astigmatism is the first and only toric daily lens with Cylinder Optimized BLINK STABILIZED® Design — meaning the four stability zones are precisely calibrated to your specific cylinder power, not a generic one-size-fits-all approach. The result: 60% more high-cylinder patients achieve improved vision compared to ACUVUE® OASYS 1-Day. That’s not a minor refinement. That’s a breakthrough. Frequently Asked Questions (FAQ) About Acuvue Contact Lenses, Acuvue Oasys & Daily Contact Lenses ❓ What is the difference between ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day and the standard Acuvue Oasys daily contact lens? ACUVUE® OASYS MAX adds two major technologies to the classic OASYS 1-Day formula: TearStable™ (all-day tear film stability) and OptiBlue™ (blue-violet light filtering). It also introduces the Cylinder Optimized BLINK STABILIZED® Design, which significantly improves stability and vision quality for high-cylinder astigmatism patients — delivering 60% better outcomes versus the standard OASYS 1-Day toric. ❓ Can I buy ACUVUE® contact lenses without a ? Yes! You can purchase your Acuvue contact lenses without needing to submit a physical . Simply place your order at contactlens365.com, enter your lens parameters (base curve, diameter, and sphere/cylinder/axis values from your last fitting), and we’ll process your order. For first-time contact lens wearers or if it’s been over a year since your last eye exam, we strongly recommend visiting your eye care professional to ensure your  is current and the lens fit is appropriate for your eyes. ❓ Do I need to have astigmatism to use Acuvue Oasys daily contact lenses? ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day for Astigmatism is specifically engineered for toric (astigmatism) correction. If you don’t have astigmatism, the spherical ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day is a better fit. Consult your eye doctor to confirm which Acuvue contact lens is right for your . ❓ What is a daily contact lens and how long does an OASYS MAX last? A daily contact lens is a single-use lens worn once and discarded at the end of the day. ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day is exactly that — wear it in the morning, remove it at night, and toss it. Never reuse or store it in solution overnight. Each box contains 30 lenses, roughly a one-month supply for one eye. ❓ What do TearStable™ and OptiBlue™ technologies actually do? TearStable™ is a moisture-locking system embedded throughout the lens material that stabilizes your natural tear film and prevents dryness during long days of screen use or in challenging environments. OptiBlue™ is a light-filtering technology that reduces blue-violet light scatter inside the eye, improving contrast and visual sharpness — especially valuable for heavy screen users and people sensitive to glare. ❓ Do Acuvue contact lenses provide UV protection? Yes. ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day offers Class 1 UV blocking — the highest UV protection classification available in any contact lens. It helps protect the cornea and interior of the eye from harmful UV-A and UV-B radiation. Note: contact lenses don’t cover the entire eye, so wearing UV-blocking sunglasses outdoors is still recommended. ❓ How many days does a 30-pack of Acuvue daily contact lenses last? Each box contains 30 lenses for one eye — approximately a 1-month supply. For both eyes, you’ll need 2 boxes. If each eye has a different , you’ll need to order two separate boxes with the appropriate parameters for each eye. ❓ Can I wear this Acuvue Oasys daily contact lens more than once? No. Like all daily contact lenses, ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day is designed for single use only. After removal, discard the lens. Reuse increases the risk of eye infection and compromises the lens’s moisture and stability performance. ❓ Is ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day suitable for first-time contact lens wearers? Absolutely. The daily contact lens format is actually ideal for first-timers — no cleaning routine, no storage, no guesswork. However, for your first fitting, a consultation with an eye care professional is strongly recommended to confirm fit, base curve, and  accuracy. ❓ OASYS MAX vs OASYS 1-Day: Which Acuvue Oasys daily contact lens should I choose? If you’re a heavy screen user, experience night driving discomfort, or have a high cylinder correction, ACUVUE® OASYS MAX is the clear choice. If your vision demands are more moderate, the standard OASYS 1-Day with HydraLuxe® Technology delivers excellent comfort at a slightly lower price point. When in doubt, your eye care professional is the best person to guide the decision. ❓ Where can I buy ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day for Astigmatism online? You can order ACUVUE® OASYS MAX 1-Day for Astigmatism directly at contactlens365.com. We offer competitive pricing, fast worldwide shipping, and a simple no-hassle ordering process. Just enter your lens parameters at checkout and we’ll take care of the rest. ACUVUE® contact lenses are vision correction devices. Always ensure your lens parameters match your most recent . If you are a first-time wearer or have not had an eye exam in over 12 months, consult your eye care professional before ordering.
